Impossibility of Accidents Subsisting in God
The author argues against the Karramiyya that accidents cannot exist in God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why accidents cannot subsist in God's essence according to the argument presented against the Karramiyya.

Core Idea
Accidents are temporal; God is eternal; they cannot coexist.

This passage addresses a key theological dispute with the Karramiyya sect, who argued that accidents could subsist in God. The author presents a logical argument based on the impossibility of combining eternal and temporal attributes. We'll examine the argument, an objection, and the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the structure: position, argument, objection, response.
The OCR is corrupt, but try to follow the logical flow.
2
Understand the main argument
Identify the core premise: eternity is negation, temporality is affirmation, and combining them is impossible. How does this refute the Karramiyya?
3
Follow the objection and response
The objection uses the analogy of the world's possibility. The response distinguishes between the possibility of description and the possibility of attribute existence. Then note the additional proof from agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسألة : لا يجوز قيام الحوادث بذات الله تعالى خلافا للكرامية) الأولية [؟] اتصافه بها لكانت تلك الصحة من لوازم ماهيته فيلم [؟] حصول تلك الصحة أزلا امكن ذلك محال اذا لوصح الأن صحة اتصافه بها أزلا يتوقف على صحة وجودها أزلا وذلك محال ، لأن الأزل عبارة عن نفى والحدوث عبارة عن ثبوتها والجمع بينهما محال . فإن قيل هذا يشكل بما أن العالم جائز الوجود لذاته ولم يلزم جواز وجوده لذلك أزلا فكذا هنا . ثم نقول صحة اتصاف الذات بالصفة عن [؟] صحة وجود الصفة فى نفسها ، ولا يلزم من ثبوت أحد يهما [؟] ثبوت الأخرى . فإنا نقول : يصبح اتصاف الذات أزلا بهذه الصفة لو كانت في نفسها ممكنة كانت الذات قابلة لهذا وهذا لا يستدعى كون الصفة في نفسها صحيحة ، ثم نقول ماذكرته إن دل على قولك فهنا ما يدل على قولنا من وجوه الأول هو أن العالم محدث فالله لم يكن فاعلا للعالم أزلا الان [؟] الفاعل ولا فعل محال ثم صار فاعلا والفاعلية صفة ثبوتية فهذا يقتضى حدوث هذه الصفة في ذات الله تعالى
(Question: It is not permissible for accidents to subsist in the essence of God Almighty, contrary to the Karramiyya.) Firstly, had He been described by them, that possibility would be a necessary concomitant of His essence, so obtaining that possibility from eternity would be possible, and that is impossible, because if now the possibility of His being described by them from eternity depends on the possibility of their existence from eternity, and that is impossible, because eternity is an expression of negation and temporality is an expression of their affirmation, and combining them is impossible. If it is said: This is problematic because the world is possible in itself, and its possibility of existence from eternity does not follow, so here too. Then we say: The possibility of the essence being described by the attribute is [something else] besides the possibility of the existence of the attribute in itself, and the affirmation of one does not entail the affirmation of the other. For we say: The essence being described from eternity by this attribute would be possible if it were possible in itself, the essence being receptive to this, and this does not require the attribute to be possible in itself. Then we say: What you have mentioned, if it indicates your view, then here is what indicates our view in some ways. The first is that the world is temporally originated, so God was not an agent of the world from eternity, because an agent without an act is impossible, then He became an agent, and agency is a positive attribute, so this necessitates the origination of this attribute in the essence of God Almighty.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the position that accidents (hawadith) cannot subsist in God's essence, contrary to the Karramiyya. The author presents a logical argument: if it were possible for God to be described by accidents, that possibility would be a necessary concomitant of His essence, and thus it would be possible from eternity. But that is impossible because eternity negates temporal origination. An objection is raised: just as the world is possible in itself but not necessarily existent from eternity, so here the possibility of description does not require actuality from eternity. The author responds by distinguishing between the possibility of the essence being described and the possibility of the attribute existing in itself; one does not entail the other. Then he provides a proof from the author's own school: the world is originated, so God was not an agent from eternity, then He became an agent, and agency is a positive attribute that is originated in God. This is the first of several arguments.

Correction: This passage shows that accidents are temporal and cannot coexist with God's eternal essence, and that agency implies a temporal attribute in God.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Ibn al-Haytham's Claim of Direction and Its Refutation
The author reports Ibn al-Haytham's directionalist view and critiques the argument from tahayyuz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn al-Haytham's claim that God is in a direction above the Throne and the initial critique based on the problem of specification.

Core Idea
Direction for God leads to impossible consequences.

This lesson begins by presenting Ibn al-Haytham's view that Allah is in a direction above the Throne with infinite distance, as well as the variations among his followers. The author then critiques the argument based on occupying space (tahayyuz) as merely repeating the claim, and discusses the difficulty of specifying a place for God by choice without an additional factor.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to the different positions attributed to Ibn al-Haytham and his followers.
The OCR is corrupt; rely on the translation.
2
Identify the main claim
Ibn al-Haytham claims God is in a direction above the Throne with infinite distance. Note the variations: some say finite distance, some say He is upon the Throne.
3
Understand the critique of the tahayyuz argument
The author says that basing the negation of direction on the concept of occupying space is just repeating the claim, not proving it.
Tahayyuz means occupying space.
4
Analyze the specification problem
If God chooses a place, this does not require an additional factor to specify it, similar to the problem of choosing between two equals.
This is a Kalām argument about divine will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصنف [؟] · ه ابن الهيضم إنه تعالى في جهة فوق الارش [؟] لا نهاية لها والبعد بينه وبين العرض أيضا غير متناه ، وقال أصحابه البعد متناه وكلهم نفوا عنه خمسا من الجهات وأثبتوا له التحت الذى هو مكان غيره ، وباقى أصحاب ابن الهيضم قالوا بكونه على العرش كما قال سائر المجسمة وبعضهم قالوا بكونه على صورة وقالوا بمجيئه وذهابه واستدلال بنى التحيز على نفى الجهة إعادة الدعوى والاختصاص بمكان هو فيه إن كان باختياره لا يقتضى أمرا زائدا تخصيصه به كما قالوا فى اختياره أحد المتساويين من غير ترجح والمكان إن لم يكن وجوديا كان كونه في المكان أزلا غير منكر على تقدير إمكان تحيره ، ومخالفة مكانه لسائر الأمكنة لا يقتضى كون مكانه موجودا ، فإن المدميات [؟] تتخالف بحسب تخالف ما ينسب إليه وإن كان المكان غير مشار إليه لم يحب [؟] من ذلك كون المتمكن غير مشار إليه فإنه من الجائز أن يصيرا هند [؟] التمكن مشارا إليهما، كما يقال فى الصورة والهيولى . والإشكال الذى أورد على المكان على تقدير كونه مشارا إليه بأنه إما أن يكون جسما أو عرضا ليس يختص بهذا الموضع بل هو وارد على أمكنة جميع الاجسام . وههنا قسم آخر وهو أن يكون خلاء لولا الجسم وقد مر فيه ما كان ينبغى أن يقال فيه والمعتمد منها أن الكائن في الجهة قابل للقسمة والأشكال وغير منفك من الأكوان ، وكل ذلك محال في حق واجب الوجود . (1) أقول الذى ذكر عام فى المواضع المتعارضة عقلا ونقلا وذلك كما ذكره.
The author [said] concerning Ibn al-Haytham that He Almighty is in a direction above the Throne, having no end, and the distance between Him and the Throne is also infinite. His companions said the distance is finite, and all of them negated five directions from Him and affirmed for Him the 'under' which is a place other than Him. The rest of Ibn al-Haytham's companions said He is upon the Throne as the rest of the corporealists said, and some said He is in a form, and they spoke of His coming and going. The argument of those who base on [the concept of] occupying space (tahayyuz) to negate direction is a repetition of the claim. The specification of a place in which He is, if it is by His choice, does not necessitate an additional matter specifying Him with it, as they said concerning His choice of one of two equals without preference. And if the place is not existent, then His being in a place from eternity is not objectionable on the assumption of the possibility of His inhabiting it. The difference of His place from other places does not necessitate that His place is existent, for non-existent things differ according to the difference of that to which they are attributed. And if the place is not an object of reference, it does not follow from that that the one located is not an object of reference, for it is possible that both the location and the located become objects of reference, as is said concerning form and matter. The problem that was raised concerning place on the assumption that it is an object of reference—that it is either a body or an accident—is not specific to this topic, but applies to the places of all bodies. Here is another section: that it is a void if not for the body, and the discussion has passed concerning what should be said about it. The relied-upon [argument] among them is that whatever is in a direction is divisible and subject to shapes and is not free from accidents (akwan), and all of that is impossible with respect to the Necessary Existent. (1) I say: what has been mentioned is general in topics that are opposed rationally and traditionally, and that is as he mentioned.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ibn al-Haytham's views on God being in a direction. The author first reports Ibn al-Haytham's claim that God is in a direction above the Throne with infinite distance, and the variations among his followers. Then he examines various arguments. He critiques the argument based on tahayyuz (occupying space) as merely repeating the claim. He discusses the possibility that God's choice of a place does not require an additional specifying factor, similar to the problem of choosing between equals. He considers the possibility of place being non-existent and argues that being in a non-existent place from eternity is not necessarily objectionable. He then addresses the issue of reference: even if place is not an object of reference, the located entity might still be an object of reference, using the analogy of form and matter. Finally, he presents the decisive argument: anything in a direction is divisible, subject to shapes, and inseparable from accidents (akwan), all of which are impossible for the Necessary Existent. The gloss notes that this is a general principle for dealing with conflicting rational and traditional evidence.

Key Terms
الجهة
ابن الهيضم
التحيز
العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God in a direction is supported by rational arguments.
Correction: The author shows that the arguments for direction are either repetitions or lead to deeper problems.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the argument from tahayyuz?
A) It is a valid proof.
B) It is a repetition of the claim.
C) It is based on scripture.
D) It establishes direction.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Haytham's directionalist view lacks a rigorous rational foundation.

?
If God’s choice of a place does not require an additional cause, then what does this say about His absolute freedom? How does this truth demand a change in how you understand God's actions in your own life—especially events you find difficult or arbitrary?

The Decisive Argument Against Directionality
The author presents the decisive rational argument against direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the decisive rational argument that anything in a direction is divisible and subject to accidents, which is impossible for the Necessary Existent.

Core Idea
Direction entails divisibility and accidents, impossible for God.

The author continues his refutation by addressing further arguments about the nature of place and reference. He then presents the critical argument: whatever is in a direction is divisible, subject to shapes, and inseparable from accidents (akwan). Since these attributes are impossible for the Necessary Existent, direction cannot be attributed to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the remainder of the passage
Read from 'والمكان إن لم يكن وجوديا' to the end. Focus on the progression of the argument.
The passage concludes with the decisive argument.
2
Analyze the arguments about place
The author discusses whether place is existent, non-existent, or an object of reference, and shows that no option forces directionality.
These are subtle metaphysical points.
3
Identify the decisive argument
The author says the relied-upon argument is that anything in a direction is divisible and not free from accidents, which is impossible for the Necessary Existent.
This is a strong theological claim.
4
Consider the concluding gloss
The author notes that this argument is general for resolving conflicting rational and traditional evidence.

Second to Fifth Arguments Against Accidents in God
The author lists four additional arguments showing why accidents cannot subsist in God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four additional arguments demonstrating why accidents cannot subsist in God, emphasizing that God's attributes must be eternal and unchanging.

Core Idea
God's attributes are eternal; temporal accidents would imply imperfection.

Imam Razi continues his systematic refutation of the possibility of accidents subsisting in God. He presents four more arguments, each targeting a different attribute—knowledge, sight/hearing, informing, and commanding—to show that if these attributes were temporal, they would entail impossibility for God. These arguments reinforce the essential eternity of God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice the repeated pattern: 'the second... the third...'.
The passage contains four distinct arguments, each introduced by a number.
2
Identify the structure of each argument
Each argument follows the same structure: it describes what God would have been like in eternity if accidents subsisted in Him, then shows that would be impossible, and then says that after the occurrence of the accident He becomes such.
The pattern is: 'God was not X, that would be impossible, then He became X.'
3
Examine each argument individually
Go through each of the four arguments (knowledge, sight/hearing, informing, commanding) and understand why the described scenario would be impossible for God.
For example, ignorance is impossible for God, so He cannot have been ignorant of the world's existence before it was created.
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
All four arguments rest on the principle that God's attributes must be eternal and unchanging. If accidents were to subsist in God, His attributes would change, which is incompatible with His perfection.
This principle is central to Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : و هو أن الله تعالى لم يكن في الأزل عالما بأن العالم موجود فإن ذلك جهل وهو على الله تعالى عمال [؟] ، ثم صار عند وجود العالم عالما بوجوده . الثالث : وهو أنه تعالى لم يكن رائيا لوجود العالم ولا سامها [؟] لوجود الأصوات لأن رؤيته موجودا مع أنه ليس موجود خطأ وهو على الله تعالى محال ، ثم أن وجود العالم والأصوات صار رائيا وسامعا . الرابع : وهو أنه تعالى لا يجوز أن يخبر فى الأزل بقوله و إنا أرسلنا نوحا ، لأن ذلك إخبار من أمر مضى وذلك في الأزل كذب وهو على الله تعالى محال ثم صار بعد إرسال نوح عليه السلام مخبرا من ذلك . الخامس : وهو أن الله تعالى لم يكن ملزما زيدا وعمرا بقوله « وأقيموا الصلاة وآتوا الزكاة » ، لأن خطاب المعدوم على سبيل الإلزام سفه وهو على الحكيم غير جائز ، ثم صار ملزما للمكلفين عند حدوثهم وحدوث الشرائط
The second: That God Almighty was not in eternity knowing that the world exists, for that would be ignorance, and that is impossible for God Almighty. Then at the existence of the world He became knowing of its existence. The third: That He Almighty was not seeing the existence of the world nor hearing the existence of sounds, because His seeing something that does not exist would be an error, and that is impossible for God Almighty. Then the existence of the world and sounds made Him seeing and hearing. The fourth: That He Almighty may not inform in eternity by His saying 'Indeed We sent Noah', because that would be informing of a past matter, and that in eternity would be a lie, and that is impossible for God Almighty. Then after sending Noah, peace be upon him, He became an informer of that. The fifth: That God Almighty was not obligating Zayd and 'Amr by His saying 'Establish prayer and give zakat', because addressing the non-existent by way of obligation is foolishness, and that is not permissible for the Wise. Then He became obligating the responsible individuals at their origination and the origination of conditions.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage lists four additional arguments (the second through fifth) that demonstrate why it is impossible for accidents to subsist in God. Each argument follows the same structure: if accidents were to subsist in God, then various attributes would be temporal, implying change and imperfection. The second argument concerns knowledge: God cannot have been ignorant of the world's existence in eternity and then become knowing. The third concerns sight and hearing: God cannot have seen or heard non-existent things, as that would be false perception. The fourth concerns speech: God cannot have informed about events that had not yet occurred, as that would be a lie. The fifth concerns command: God cannot address non-existent beings with obligations, as that would be foolish. These arguments show that if accidents (like knowledge, sight, etc.) were to subsist in God and be temporal, it would entail unacceptable consequences.

الرؤية

الإخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attributes are temporal and can be acquired over time.
Correction: The passage argues that such attributes would entail imperfection (ignorance, error, lie, foolishness) and are therefore impossible for God. God's attributes are eternal and unchanging.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the arguments listed in this passage?
A) God was not knowing the world's existence from eternity.
B) God was not seeing or hearing non-existent things.
C) God did not create the world from eternity.
D) God did not address non-existent beings with obligations.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal; temporal accidents cannot subsist in Him because they would imply change and imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Will you trust His eternal knowledge for one specific worry right now?
?
God's seeing and hearing are eternal and unchanging — He sees and hears all, not after the fact but from eternity. Does your private life reflect the reality that God's sight of your actions is not added later but is always present? What habit would you stop or start today because of this truth?
?
God's command to pray and give zakat is eternal and addressed to every responsible being. Do you live as if that command was given specifically to you, and that it has always been binding? What concrete step will you take today to obey that eternal command more fully?

Change is in Relations, Not in God
The author answers objections about temporal attributes and explains relational change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why changes in how God is described (e.g., becoming Creator after creation) are changes in relations, not in God's essence or attributes.

Core Idea
Relations change; God's essence and attributes remain unchanged.

This passage addresses a key objection against Divine immutability: if God is called 'Creator' only after creation, does that imply a change in God? The author explains that what changes is the relation between the attribute (e.g., power) and its object, not the attribute itself. Understanding this distinction clarifies how God can be described with new relations without implying change in His essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its full translation. Notice how the author dismisses the objection about the world's possibility before creation.
The OCR is corrupt; rely on the translation for clarity.
2
Identify the key principle
Find the sentence: 'what changes is the relation of attributes to things, not the attributes themselves.' This is the core of the answer.
The Arabic phrase: 'أن المتغير إضافة الصفات إلى الأشياء لا نفس الصفات'.
3
Understand why relations are non-existent
The author states that relations have no external existence (لا وجود لها في الخارج). This means they are mental constructs, not real things, so their change does not affect God's essence.
This is a key Ashʿarī position.
4
Follow the objection and counter-answer
Read how the author responds to the objection that 'the possibility of being described is different from the possibility of the attribute.' He argues that the former depends on the latter, but the possibility of an act does not require the actual existence of the effect.
This shows the subtlety of kalam reasoning.
5
Conclude with the decisive proof
The author concludes that the reliable argument is that change in God would imply being affected (infiʿāl), which is impossible for God.
This links to the broader theme of Divine simplicity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب : أما صحة العالم فغير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نقيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه لا بالصحه ولا بالامتناع . قوله : صحة الاتصاف بالوصف غير صحة الصدفة [؟] وجود قلنا : لا نزاع فيه لكن الأولى متوقفة على الثانية لأن صحة الاتصاف به متوقفة على تحققه وتحققه متوقف على وجوده ، وأما المعارضات فالضابط فيها شيء واحد وهو، أن المتغير إضافة الصفات إلى الأشباء لا نفس الصفات ، وقد دللنا فيما تقدم على أن الإضافة لا وجود لها في الخارج (1) أقول : صحة الاتصاف إضافة و الإضافات عنده غير موجودة وغير الموجود لا يمكن حصوله في الأزل فلا يلزم من صحة اتصافه بها حصولها في الأزل ولا فى غير الأزل بزعمه ، وأيضاً لو كانت صفة الاتصاف موجودة لا يكفى كونها أزلية . له : في الاعتراض صحة الانصاف [؟] غير صحة وجود الصفة ولا يلزم من ثبوت أحدهما أزلا ثبوت الأخرى صحيح . وجوابه : بأن صحة الانفاق [؟] يتوقف على صحة وجوده ليس بشيء لأن صحة حدوث المقدور من القادر لا يتوقف على وجود المقدور ولا على صحة وجوده مطلقا ، بل يتوقف على صحة وجود مقدور لذاته ، وإن امتنع وجود مقدوره لعائق أو فوات شرط لم يضر ذلك في صحة المقدور منه . وقوله : صحة القائم [؟] غير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نفيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه بالصحة غير صحيح لأن الخلق كان في الأزل بحيث يصح صدور أثر منه فيما لايزال ، وليس المراد بصحة العالم في الأزل إلا صحة صدور ذلك الأثر فيما لا يزال . وأما المعارضات فجوابها ما ذكره، والإضاءات [؟] يمكن أن تتغير وتكثر بسبب تغير ما إليه الإضافة وتكثره واعلم أن المعتمد في هذا المقام الاستدلال بامتناع التغير عليه معه لامتناع انفعاله في ذاته و
And the answer: As for the possibility of the world, it is not relevant, because the world before its origination was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged either as possible or impossible. His statement: 'The possibility of being described by the attribute is different from the possibility of the existence of the attribute.' We say: there is no dispute about that, but the former depends on the latter, because the possibility of being described by it depends on its actualization, and its actualization depends on its existence. As for the objections, the principle is one thing: what changes is the relation of attributes to things, not the attributes themselves, and we have proven previously that relation has no external existence. (1) I say: The possibility of being described is a relation, and relations according to him are non-existent, and what is non-existent cannot be obtained in eternity, so it does not follow from the possibility of His being described by them that they are obtained in eternity or outside eternity according to his claim. Also, even if the attribute of being described existed, its being eternal would not suffice. To him: In the objection, the possibility of being described is different from the possibility of the existence of the attribute, and it is correct that the affirmation of one in eternity does not entail the affirmation of the other. And his answer: that the possibility of [the attribute] depends on the possibility of its existence is not valid, because the possibility of the origination of the effect from the agent does not depend on the existence of the effect nor on its possibility absolutely, but depends on the possibility of the existence of an effect in itself. And if the existence of his effect is prevented by an obstacle or loss of a condition, that does not harm the possibility of the effect from him. And his statement: 'The possibility of the existing is not relevant' because the world before its origination was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged as possible, is not correct, because the creation was in eternity such that an effect could issue from Him in the future, and what is meant by the possibility of the world in eternity is only the possibility of the issuance of that effect in the future. As for the objections, their answer is what he mentioned. And relations can change and multiply due to the change and multiplication of that to which the relation is directed. Know that the relied-upon argument in this topic is to prove the impossibility of change upon Him because of the impossibility of being affected in His essence.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage contains the overall answer to the objections raised and a detailed discussion of relational attributes. The author begins by dismissing the objection about the world's possibility: the world before creation was non-existent, so it cannot be judged. He then addresses the distinction between the possibility of being described and the possibility of the attribute itself, affirming the distinction but arguing that the former depends on the latter. The key principle: when God is said to 'become' knowing or seeing, what changes is the relation of the attribute to the object, not the attribute itself. Relations have no external existence. The gloss adds that if relations are non-existent, they cannot be eternal. Further objections are answered: the possibility of a potential act does not depend on actual existence. The author concludes that the decisive argument is the impossibility of change in God's essence, as change implies being affected (infi'al).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's attributes like 'Creator' and 'Provider' begin to exist when He creates or provides, implying change in God.
Correction: The attributes themselves are eternal and unchanging; only the relation (iḍāfa) of the attribute to its object changes. Relations have no external reality, so no change occurs in God's essence.

Key Takeaway
God's attributes are eternal and unchanging; only the relations between attributes and their objects change, and relations have no external reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
When you experience spiritual dryness, you sense a 'change' in your connection to God. But this lesson teaches that God's attributes are unchanged. Five Objections to Timeless Divine Attributes
Five objections alleging change in divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five objections that claim God's attributes would have to change when the world is created, challenging the doctrine of timeless attributes.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes seem incompatible with new facts about creation.

Before presenting his answer, Imam Razi lists five objections that a critic might raise. Each objection takes a specific divine attribute—knowledge, sight, speech, or command—and argues that if it were eternal, then certain statements about creation would be impossible or false in eternity, implying change in God. Recognizing the pattern helps us appreciate the precision of the response.

Guided Path
1
Read each objection carefully
Read the five objections in order. Notice how each one begins with 'God was not in eternity...' and ends with 'then He became...'.
The objects of knowledge, sight, etc. are temporal.
2
Identify the common logical structure
Each objection claims that an eternal attribute cannot become true of a temporal object without change in God. Identify the pattern: premise, impossibility, then change.
The pattern is: In eternity, attribute X does not apply to object Y (impossible if it were otherwise); after Y exists, attribute X does apply. Therefore God changed.
3
Note the specific attributes and objects
List the attributes: knowledge, sight, hearing, informing, commanding. The objects: the world's existence, the world and sounds, the sending of Noah, the obligation of prayer.
Each objection targets a different attribute to show the problem is general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : و هو أن الله تعالى لم يكن في الأزل عالما بأن العالم موجود فإن ذلك جهل وهو على الله تعالى محال ، ثم صار عند وجود العالم عالما بوجوده .
الثالث : وهو أنه تعالى لم يكن رائيا لوجود العالم ولا سامعا لوجود الأصوات لأن رؤيته موجودا مع أنه ليس موجود خطأ وهو على الله تعالى محال ، ثم عند وجود العالم والأصوات صار رائيا وسامعا .
الرابع : وهو أنه تعالى لا يجوز أن يخبر في الأزل بقوله و إنا أرسلنا نوحا ، لأن ذلك إخبار عن أمر مضى وذلك في الأزل كذب وهو على الله تعالى محال ثم صار بعد إرسال نوح عليه السلام مخبرا بذلك .
الخامس : وهو أن الله تعالى لم يكن ملزما زيدا وعمرا بقوله « وأقيموا الصلاة وآتوا الزكاة » ، لأن خطاب المعدوم على سبيل الإلزام سفه وهو على الحكيم غير جائز ، ثم صار ملزما للمكلفين عند حدوثهم وحدوث الشرائط .
والجواب : أما صحة العالم فغير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نقيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه لا بالصحة ولا بالامتناع . قوله : صحة الاتصاف بالوصف غير صحة وجود الصفة . قلنا : لا نزاع فيه لكن الأولى متوقفة على الثانية لأن صحة الاتصاف به متوقفة على تحققه وتحققه متوقف على وجوده . وأما المعارضات فالضابط فيها شيء واحد وهو ، أن المتغير إضافة الصفات إلى الأشياء لا نفس الصفات ، وقد دللنا فيما تقدم على أن الإضافة لا وجود لها في الخارج . (1) أقول : صحة الاتصاف إضافة و الإضافات عنده غير موجودة وغير الموجود لا يمكن حصوله في الأزل فلا يلزم من صحة اتصافه بها حصولها في الأزل ولا فى غير الأزل بزعمه ، وأيضاً لو كانت صفة الاتصاف موجودة لا يكفى كونها أزلية . له : في الاعتراض صحة الاتصاف غير صحة وجود الصفة ولا يلزم من ثبوت أحدهما أزلا ثبوت الأخرى صحيح . وجوابه : بأن صحة الاتصاف يتوقف على صحة وجوده ليس بشيء لأن صحة حدوث المقدور من القادر لا يتوقف على وجود المقدور ولا على صحة وجوده مطلقا ، بل يتوقف على صحة وجود مقدور لذاته ، وإن امتنع وجود مقدوره لعائق أو فوات شرط لم يضر ذلك في صحة المقدور منه وقوله : صحة العالم غير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نفيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه بالصحة غير صحيح لأن الخلق كان في الأزل بحيث يصح صدور أثر منه فيما لايزال ، وليس المراد بصحة العالم في الأزل إلا صحة صدور ذلك الأثر فيما لا يزال . وأما المعارضات فجوابها ما ذكره، والإضافات يمكن أن تتغير وتكثر بسبب تغير ما إليه الإضافة وتكثره . واعلم أن المعتمد في هذا المقام الاستدلال بامتناع التغير عليه معه لامتناع انفعاله في ذاته .
The second: that God Almighty was not in eternity knowing that the world exists, for that is ignorance, and it is impossible for God Almighty; then at the existence of the world He became knowing of its existence. The third: that He Almighty was not seeing the existence of the world nor hearing the existence of sounds, because His seeing something that does not exist is an error and it is impossible for God Almighty; then with the existence of the world and sounds He became seeing and hearing. The fourth: that He Almighty is not allowed to inform in eternity by His saying 'Indeed We sent Noah', because that is informing about a past matter, and that in eternity is a lie, and it is impossible for God Almighty; then after sending Noah (peace be upon him) He became informing of that. The fifth: that God Almighty was not obligating Zayd and 'Amr by His saying 'Establish prayer and give zakah', because addressing the non-existent by way of obligation is foolishness and it is not permissible for the Wise; then He became obligating the responsible individuals at the time of their occurrence and the occurrence of conditions. And the answer: As for the validity of the world, it is not relevant because the world before its occurrence was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged as valid or impossible. His statement: 'The validity of being described by a description is not the same as the validity of the existence of the description.' We say: There is no dispute about that, but the former depends on the latter, because the validity of being described by it depends on its realization, and its realization depends on its existence. As for the counterarguments, the principle in them is one thing: that what changes is the relation of attributes to things, not the attributes themselves; and we have demonstrated previously that relation has no existence in the external world. (1) I say: The validity of being described is a relation, and relations according to him are non-existent, and what is non-existent cannot obtain in eternity, so it does not follow from the validity of His being described with them that they obtain in eternity or in non-eternity, according to his claim. Also, if the quality of being described were existent, its being eternal would not suffice. To him: In the objection, 'the validity of being described is not the validity of the existence of the description,' and it does not follow from the establishment of one of them in eternity the establishment of the other. That is correct. And his answer: that the validity of being described depends on the validity of its existence is nothing, because the validity of the occurrence of the potential from the capable does not depend on the existence of the potential nor on the validity of its existence absolutely, but depends on the validity of the existence of a potential in itself; and if the existence of its potential is prevented by an obstacle or loss of a condition, that does not harm the validity of the potential from him. And his statement: 'The validity of the world is not relevant because the world before its occurrence was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged as valid' is not correct, because creation in eternity was such that an effect could validly issue from it in the future, and what is meant by the validity of the world in eternity is only the validity of the issuance of that effect in the future. As for the counterarguments, their answer is what he mentioned, and relations can change and multiply due to the change and multiplication of what they are related to. And know that the relied-upon in this context is the proof by the impossibility of change upon Him with change, due to the impossibility of His being affected in His essence.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents five objections against the possibility of God having attributes that change with the creation of the world, and then provides an answer. The objections are: (1) God was not knowing the world's existence in eternity, but became so after creation, implying change. (2) He was not seeing or hearing the world/sounds, but became so after creation. (3) He could not truthfully inform about sending Noah in eternity, but could after sending. (4) He could not command non-existent individuals, but could after their existence. Each objection claims that if attributes are eternal, they cannot become true later, suggesting divine change. The answer begins by arguing that the validity of the world before creation is not relevant because it was non-existent; judgments of validity or impossibility do not apply. It then distinguishes between 'validity of being described' and 'validity of existence of the description'—the former depends on the latter, but the existence depends on the object's existence. The key principle is that what changes is not the attribute itself, but the relation (إضافة) of the attribute to the object. Relations have no external existence, so no change in God's essence occurs. The footnote (أقول) elaborates: the validity of being described is a relation, non-existent externally, so it does not require eternal existence. It also addresses a subtle objection about the dependency of the validity of being described on the validity of existence, arguing that the potential for an effect from a capable agent does not require the actual existence of the effect. Finally, the passage concludes that the relied-upon proof is the impossibility of change in God due to the impossibility of His being passive (انفعال).

Key Terms
تغير (change)
جهل (ignorance)
كذب (lie)
سفه (foolishness)
معدوم (non-existent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objections prove that God's attributes actually change over time.
Correction: The objections only show a problem if attributes themselves change. The answer will argue that only the relation (إضافة) changes, preserving immutability.

Checkpoint
What is the common pattern in all five objections?
A) They claim God's attributes are not eternal.
B) They claim that an eternal attribute cannot become true of a temporal object without change.
C) They claim that God's knowledge is limited.
D) They claim that God's attributes are created.

Key Takeaway
These five objections challenge the doctrine of timeless attributes by showing an apparent incompatibility with temporal facts, all following the same logical pattern.

How does that truth challenge your tendency to doubt His awareness? Will you commit to trusting that His knowledge of your life is as perfect in this moment as it was before creation?

Does knowing that God's command to you was issued before you were born change how you view your responsibility to obey? What would it mean for you to live today as if you are answering a call that has been waiting for you since eternity?

Answer: Only Relations Change
Answer: change is in relations, not attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinction between the attribute itself and its relation to objects, and how only relations change without affecting God's essence.

Core Idea
What changes is the relation of attributes to objects, not the attributes.

Imam Razi now provides the answer to the five objections. He first dismisses a preliminary objection about the validity of the world before creation, then introduces a crucial distinction between 'validity of being described' and 'validity of existence of the description'. The core principle is that change occurs only in the relations (إضافات) of attributes to objects, and relations have no external existence. A footnote elaborates on this principle and addresses a subtle counter-argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer and footnote
Read the entire answer, including the footnote marked (1). Notice the different parts: dismissal of the world's validity, the distinction between two validities, the principle of relation, and the footnote's discussion.
The footnote begins with 'أقول' and offers additional analysis.
2
Understand the key distinction
The author distinguishes between 'validity of being described' (صحة الاتصاف) and 'validity of existence of the description' (صحة وجود الصفة). The former depends on the latter, but the existence of the description depends on the object's existence.
This distinction helps show that the attribute's existence is not required in eternity.
3
Grasp the principle of relational change
The answer states: what changes is the relation (إضافة) of attributes to things, not the attributes themselves. Relations have no external existence, so no real change in God.
This is the core refutation of the objections.
4
Analyze the footnote's argument
The footnote (أقول) argues that the validity of being described is itself a relation, and relations are non-existent externally. It also critiques a subtle point about dependency of validity.
This strengthens the answer by showing that even the 'validity of being described' is not an existent attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : و هو أن الله تعالى لم يكن في الأزل عالما بأن العالم موجود فإن ذلك جهل وهو على الله تعالى محال ، ثم صار عند وجود العالم عالما بوجوده .
الثالث : وهو أنه تعالى لم يكن رائيا لوجود العالم ولا سامعا لوجود الأصوات لأن رؤيته موجودا مع أنه ليس موجود خطأ وهو على الله تعالى محال ، ثم عند وجود العالم والأصوات صار رائيا وسامعا .
الرابع : وهو أنه تعالى لا يجوز أن يخبر في الأزل بقوله و إنا أرسلنا نوحا ، لأن ذلك إخبار عن أمر مضى وذلك في الأزل كذب وهو على الله تعالى محال ثم صار بعد إرسال نوح عليه السلام مخبرا بذلك .
الخامس : وهو أن الله تعالى لم يكن ملزما زيدا وعمرا بقوله « وأقيموا الصلاة وآتوا الزكاة » ، لأن خطاب المعدوم على سبيل الإلزام سفه وهو على الحكيم غير جائز ، ثم صار ملزما للمكلفين عند حدوثهم وحدوث الشرائط .
والجواب : أما صحة العالم فغير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نقيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه لا بالصحة ولا بالامتناع . قوله : صحة الاتصاف بالوصف غير صحة وجود الصفة . قلنا : لا نزاع فيه لكن الأولى متوقفة على الثانية لأن صحة الاتصاف به متوقفة على تحققه وتحققه متوقف على وجوده . وأما المعارضات فالضابط فيها شيء واحد وهو ، أن المتغير إضافة الصفات إلى الأشياء لا نفس الصفات ، وقد دللنا فيما تقدم على أن الإضافة لا وجود لها في الخارج . (1) أقول : صحة الاتصاف إضافة و الإضافات عنده غير موجودة وغير الموجود لا يمكن حصوله في الأزل فلا يلزم من صحة اتصافه بها حصولها في الأزل ولا فى غير الأزل بزعمه ، وأيضاً لو كانت صفة الاتصاف موجودة لا يكفى كونها أزلية . له : في الاعتراض صحة الاتصاف غير صحة وجود الصفة ولا يلزم من ثبوت أحدهما أزلا ثبوت الأخرى صحيح . وجوابه : بأن صحة الاتصاف يتوقف على صحة وجوده ليس بشيء لأن صحة حدوث المقدور من القادر لا يتوقف على وجود المقدور ولا على صحة وجوده مطلقا ، بل يتوقف على صحة وجود مقدور لذاته ، وإن امتنع وجود مقدوره لعائق أو فوات شرط لم يضر ذلك في صحة المقدور منه وقوله : صحة العالم غير واردة لأن العالم قبل حدوثه كان نفيا محضا فلا يمكن الحكم عليه بالصحة غير صحيح لأن الخلق كان في الأزل بحيث يصح صدور أثر منه فيما لايزال ، وليس المراد بصحة العالم في الأزل إلا صحة صدور ذلك الأثر فيما لا يزال . وأما المعارضات فجوابها ما ذكره، والإضافات يمكن أن تتغير وتكثر بسبب تغير ما إليه الإضافة وتكثره . واعلم أن المعتمد في هذا المقام الاستدلال بامتناع التغير عليه معه لامتناع انفعاله في ذاته .
The second: that God Almighty was not in eternity knowing that the world exists, for that is ignorance, and it is impossible for God Almighty; then at the existence of the world He became knowing of its existence. The third: that He Almighty was not seeing the existence of the world nor hearing the existence of sounds, because His seeing something that does not exist is an error and it is impossible for God Almighty; then with the existence of the world and sounds He became seeing and hearing. The fourth: that He Almighty is not allowed to inform in eternity by His saying 'Indeed We sent Noah', because that is informing about a past matter, and that in eternity is a lie, and it is impossible for God Almighty; then after sending Noah (peace be upon him) He became informing of that. The fifth: that God Almighty was not obligating Zayd and 'Amr by His saying 'Establish prayer and give zakah', because addressing the non-existent by way of obligation is foolishness and it is not permissible for the Wise; then He became obligating the responsible individuals at the time of their occurrence and the occurrence of conditions. And the answer: As for the validity of the world, it is not relevant because the world before its occurrence was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged as valid or impossible. His statement: 'The validity of being described by a description is not the same as the validity of the existence of the description.' We say: There is no dispute about that, but the former depends on the latter, because the validity of being described by it depends on its realization, and its realization depends on its existence. As for the counterarguments, the principle in them is one thing: that what changes is the relation of attributes to things, not the attributes themselves; and we have demonstrated previously that relation has no existence in the external world. (1) I say: The validity of being described is a relation, and relations according to him are non-existent, and what is non-existent cannot obtain in eternity, so it does not follow from the validity of His being described with them that they obtain in eternity or in non-eternity, according to his claim. Also, if the quality of being described were existent, its being eternal would not suffice. To him: In the objection, 'the validity of being described is not the validity of the existence of the description,' and it does not follow from the establishment of one of them in eternity the establishment of the other. That is correct. And his answer: that the validity of being described depends on the validity of its existence is nothing, because the validity of the occurrence of the potential from the capable does not depend on the existence of the potential nor on the validity of its existence absolutely, but depends on the validity of the existence of a potential in itself; and if the existence of its potential is prevented by an obstacle or loss of a condition, that does not harm the validity of the potential from him. And his statement: 'The validity of the world is not relevant because the world before its occurrence was pure non-existence, so it cannot be judged as valid' is not correct, because creation in eternity was such that an effect could validly issue from it in the future, and what is meant by the validity of the world in eternity is only the validity of the issuance of that effect in the future. As for the counterarguments, their answer is what he mentioned, and relations can change and multiply due to the change and multiplication of what they are related to. And know that the relied-upon in this context is the proof by the impossibility of change upon Him with change, due to the impossibility of His being affected in His essence.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents five objections against the possibility of God having attributes that change with the creation of the world, and then provides an answer. The objections are: (1) God was not knowing the world's existence in eternity, but became so after creation, implying change. (2) He was not seeing or hearing the world/sounds, but became so after creation. (3) He could not truthfully inform about sending Noah in eternity, but could after sending. (4) He could not command non-existent individuals, but could after their existence. Each objection claims that if attributes are eternal, they cannot become true later, suggesting divine change. The answer begins by arguing that the validity of the world before creation is not relevant because it was non-existent; judgments of validity or impossibility do not apply. It then distinguishes between 'validity of being described' and 'validity of existence of the description'—the former depends on the latter, but the existence depends on the object's existence. The key principle is that what changes is not the attribute itself, but the relation (إضافة) of the attribute to the object. Relations have no external existence, so no change in God's essence occurs. The footnote (أقول) elaborates: the validity of being described is a relation, non-existent externally, so it does not require eternal existence. It also addresses a subtle objection about the dependency of the validity of being described on the validity of existence, arguing that the potential for an effect from a capable agent does not require the actual existence of the effect. Finally, the passage concludes that the relied-upon proof is the impossibility of change in God due to the impossibility of His being passive (انفعال).

Key Terms
إضافة (relation)
صحة الاتصاف (validity of being described)
صحة وجود الصفة (validity of existence of the attribute)
نفي محض (pure non-existence)
انفعال (being affected)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The answer implies that God's attributes themselves come into existence at the time of creation.
Correction: The answer clearly states that the attributes themselves do not change; only the relation (إضافة) changes, and relations are not real existents.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what actually changes when God's knowledge of the world becomes actual?
A) The attribute of knowledge itself changes.
B) The world changes from non-existence to existence.
C) The relation of God's knowledge to the world changes.
D) God's essence undergoes a change.

Key Takeaway
The answer to the five objections is that only relations (إضافات) of attributes to objects change; these relations have no external existence, so God's essence and attributes remain immutable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God's attributes like His mercy and justice are absolutely unchanging, does it convict you that your own emotions and commitments fluctuate? How can you anchor your trust in His unchanging nature rather than your own variable feelings?
?
The passage teaches that relations change but God does not. Are there moments when you secretly wish God would change His mind about something in your life? What does that reveal about your understanding of His perfect wisdom?
?
If God is never affected by His creation (لا انفعال), then your sins do not 'hurt' Him or change His essence. Does that make you take sin more lightly, or does it deepen your gratitude that He still responds with mercy and justice without being diminished? What commitment does this demand of you?

The Impossibility of Pain and Pleasure for God
Razi affirms consensus on pain's impossibility and refutes philosophers on intellectual pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical Islamic theology affirms the impossibility of pain and pleasure for God, and how the philosophers' claim of intellectual pleasure is refuted by consensus and rational argument.

Core Idea
Pain and pleasure, even intellectual, require passivity, which is impossible for God.

Imam Razi addresses a key attribute of God: His transcendence above physical and emotional changes. While all Muslims agree that God cannot suffer pain, some philosophers argued that He could experience intellectual pleasure. This lesson examines the rational proofs and the appeal to consensus that settle the matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the literal translation. Notice the flow from consensus to proof to objection to answer.
2
Identify the two main claims
The passage opens with consensus on pain's impossibility, then presents the dispute over intellectual pleasure. Identify these two stances.
3
Trace the author's main proof
Find the argument that if pleasure is eternal it demands the pre-creation of the pleasurable thing; if temporal it makes God a locus of events. Understand the dilemma.
This is the 'relied-upon' proof.
4
Understand the objection and answer
The philosophers claim pleasure arises from God's own perfection, not from creation. The author answers that consensus rejects this, and God is free from passivity.
The footnote adds nuance about the proof's conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : اتفق الكل على استحالة الألم على الله تعالى وأما اللذات العقلية فثبت أثبتها الفلاسفة والباقون ينكرونها . لنا أن اللذة والألم من توابع اعتدال المزاج وتنافره وذلك لا يعقل إلا في الجسم وهو ضعيف ، لأنه يقال هب أن اعتدال المزاج يوجب اللذة لكن لا يلزم من انتفاء السبب الواحد انتفاء المسبب، والمعتمد أن تلك اللذة إن كانت قديمة وهى داعية إلى فعل الملتذ به وجب أن يكون موجدا للملتذ به قبل أن أوجده ، لأن الداعي إلى إيجاده قبل ذلك موجود، ولا مانع، لكن إيجاد الشيء قبل إيجاده محال، وإن كانت حادثة كان محل الحوادث . قالت الفلاسفة : هذه الدلالة لا تبطل الألم، وأما اللذة فنحن لا نقول إنه يلتذ بخلق شيء آخر لسكنا ندعى أن عليه لكماله المطلق يوجب اللذة ، والدلالة التي ذكرتموها لا تدفع ما قلناه ، وتقريره أن كل من تصور في نفسه كمالا فرح ومن تصور في نفسه نقصانا تألم ، وإذا كان كماله سبحانه وتعالى أعظم الكمالات وعليه بكماله أجل العلوم فلم لا يجوز أن يستلزم ذلك أعظم اللذات . والجواب أنه باطل بإجماع الأمة وكذلك الألم (1) أقول : اللذة والألم اللذان من توابع المزاج فلا شك في استحالتهما عليه تعالى ، وقوله إن كانت اللذة قديمة وجب أن يوجد الملتذ به قبل أن أوجده، لأن تقدم داعى اللذة لازم على داعي الإيجاد ، إنما كان الملتذ به من فعله ، وعلى تقديره يصلح لو كان داعي الإيجاد متجددا مغايرا لداعى اللذة ، أو كان داعي الإيجاد أيضا قديما لكنه غير كاف في الإيجاد إلا بعد وجود الملتذ به ، وإذا كان داعى اللذة داعي الإيجاد بعينه لم يلزم الخلاف المذكور. وقوله : هذه الدلالة لا تبطل الألم يتعين إذ ليس إليه داع فلا يلزم هذا الخلف . وقوله : الفلاسفة يقولون عليه بكماله وتقرير اللذة والألم اللذين موجبهما العلم بالكمال والنقصان في حقه تعالى ليس بفيد ، لأنه منزه عن الانفعال والتمسك بإجماع الأمة يفيد في عدم إطلاق لفظي اللذة والألم عليه تعالى ، لأن كل صفة لا يقارنها الإذن الشرعى لا يوصف تعالى بها إلا في العين الذي ادعاه الفلاسفة ، فالإجماع حاصل ونفى الألم عنه تعالى لا يحتاج إلى بيان لأن الألم إدراك مناف ولا منافي له تعالى .
Issue: All have agreed on the impossibility of pain for God Almighty. As for intellectual pleasures, the philosophers affirmed them while the rest deny them. Our proof: that pleasure and pain are among the consequences of balance and imbalance of temperament, and that is only conceivable in a body—and this is weak, because it is said: Grant that balance of temperament necessitates pleasure, but the absence of one cause does not necessitate the absence of the effect. And the relied-upon is that if that pleasure is eternal and it is a motivator for the act of the pleasurable thing, then He must be bringing into existence the pleasurable thing before He brings it into existence, because the motivator to bring it into existence before that exists, and there is no impediment; but bringing something into existence before its existence is impossible. And if it is temporal, then it would be a locus of temporal events. The philosophers said: This proof does not refute pain. As for pleasure, we do not say that He takes pleasure in creating something else; rather we claim that He, due to His absolute perfection, necessitates pleasure, and the proof you mentioned does not refute what we said. Its exposition: that everyone who conceives in himself perfection rejoices, and who conceives in himself deficiency suffers pain; and since His perfection (glorified and exalted) is the greatest of perfections, and His knowledge of His perfection is the greatest of sciences, so why is it not possible that this entails the greatest pleasures? The answer: that it is false by the consensus of the community, and likewise pain. (1) I say: Pleasure and pain that are consequences of temperament are unquestionably impossible for Him Almighty. And his statement: 'If the pleasure is eternal, then He must bring the pleasurable thing into existence before He brings it into existence, because the priority of the motivator of pleasure over the motivator of bringing into existence is necessary'—this only applies if the pleasurable thing is from His act; and on that supposition, it would be valid if the motivator of bringing into existence was renewed and different from the motivator of pleasure, or if the motivator of bringing into existence was also eternal but not sufficient for bringing into existence except after the existence of the pleasurable thing. And if the motivator of pleasure is the same as the motivator of bringing into existence, then the mentioned absurdity does not follow. And his statement: 'This proof does not refute pain' is decisive, since there is no motivator for it, so this absurdity does not follow. And his statement: 'The philosophers say: He, due to His perfection, and the exposition of pleasure and pain whose cause is knowledge of perfection and deficiency in His right' is not beneficial, because He is free from passivity, and adherence to the consensus of the community is beneficial in not applying the terms 'pleasure' and 'pain' to Him Almighty, because no attribute that is not accompanied by religious permission is attributed to Him Almighty except in the specific sense that the philosophers claim. So consensus is established, and the negation of pain from Him Almighty needs no explanation because pain is a perception of something harmful, and there is nothing harmful to Him Almighty.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument affirming consensus on the impossibility of pain for God, and then addressing the philosophers' claim that intellectual pleasure is possible for God. The author first states the consensus. Then he gives a proof: pain and pleasure are tied to bodily temperament (اعتدال المزاج) and its imbalance, which only applies to bodies. This is called weak because the absence of one cause does not negate the effect; pleasure might have another cause. So the relied-upon argument is: if that pleasure is eternal, it would obligate God to create the pleasurable object before creation, which is absurd; if it is temporal, God would be a locus of accidents. The philosophers object that they do not claim God's pleasure comes from creating something else, but from His own perfection. They argue that knowledge of one's perfection produces pleasure, and since God's perfection is greatest, pleasure necessarily follows. The answer is that this is false by consensus (إجماع الأمة), and also pain is negated. The footnote (أقول) explains that the proof about eternal pleasure creating a paradox only holds if the motivator for pleasure is distinct from the motivator for creation; if they are the same, no absurdity. However, any pleasure/ pain based on temperament is impossible. Moreover, even the philosophers' claim of intellectual pleasure is rejected because God is free from passivity (انفعال), and consensus prohibits applying these terms without religious permission.

Key Terms
الألم
اللذة
اعتدال المزاج
إجماع الأمة
الانفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellectual pleasure is possible for God because it does not involve a body.
Correction: All pleasure involves passivity (انفعال) or a causal chain tied to temperament; God is free from both, and consensus also rejects the application of these terms.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author gives to reject the philosophers' claim that God experiences intellectual pleasure?
A) It contradicts the consensus of the Muslim community.
B) It would imply that God has a body.
C) It cannot be proven from revelation.
D) It would require God to create something to enjoy.

Key Takeaway
God is free from all forms of pain and pleasure, as affirmed by consensus and reason, because they entail passivity or temporality incompatible with His essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi argues that even the 'highest' pleasure—from knowledge of perfection—is impossible for God because it implies passivity. When you pray or worship, do you secretly imagine that your actions cause a change in God's emotional state? How would your worship change if you truly believed God is beyond all pleasure and pain?
?
The philosophers thought that God must rejoice in His perfection. But Razi says this is false by consensus. Do you sometimes assume God feels pleased with your obedience as a human would? What would it mean for your relationship with God to accept that He does not experience pleasure—that His 'pleasure' is a metaphor for His will to reward?
?
If pain is impossible for God, then the fear of God's displeasure cannot be a fear of Him feeling hurt or angry. What is it that you truly fear when you think of displeasing God? How does Razi's argument challenge you to purify your concept of God from anthropomorphic emotions?

The Proof that God is Qadir (Powerful) from Contingency
Razi divides the agent of the world into two categories and refutes the first to prove God's free agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God must be a free agent (Qadir) and how it disproves necessitarian views.

Core Idea
God's power is proven by the impossibility of a necessitating cause for the world.

Razi begins by stating the consensus that God is Qadir, then provides a logical proof. He argues that the world's dependence on an agent forces us to choose between two types of agency. By refuting the necessitating cause, only the free agent remains, which is the very meaning of Qadir. This lesson walks through that reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of agents
Read the passage and locate where Razi divides the agent into two categories. Notice the phrase 'إما أن يعال صدر الأثر عنه مع امتناع أن لا يصدر أو صدر مع جواز أن لا يصدر'.
These are the necessitating cause and the free agent.
2
Understand why the necessitating cause is impossible
Follow Razi's refutation: if the agent's influence requires no condition, then the agent's eternity would necessitate the world's eternity. If it requires a condition, that condition is either eternal (same problem) or originated, leading to infinite regress.
Infinite regress and an infinite series of originated events are both impossible.
3
Trace the infinite regress argument
Razi argues that if the condition is originated, then its own origination requires another agent, and so on, leading to either simultaneous infinite regress or an infinite sequence without a first, both absurd.
This eliminates the possibility of a necessitating cause altogether.
4
Conclude that the agent must be free
With the first possibility invalidated, the second must hold: the agent produces the effect with the possibility of not producing it. This is exactly what Qadir means.
Thus God is Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : اتفق الكل على أنه تعالى قادر خلافا الجمهور الفلاسفة لنا أنه ثبت افتقار العالم إلى مؤثر فذلك المؤثر إما أن يعال صدر الأثر عنه مع امتناع أن لا يصدر أو صدر مع جواز أن لا يصدر ، والأول باطل لأن تأثيره في وجود العالم إن لم يتوقف على شرط لزم من قدمه قدم العالم وقد أبطلناه ، وإن توقف على شرط فذلك الشرط إن كان قديما عاد الإلزام ، فإن كان محمد ثا كان الكلام في حدوثه كالكلام فى الأول وازم التسلسل إما معا وهو محال أو لا إلى أول فيلزم منه حوادث لا أول لها وهو محال ، ولما بطل هذا القسم ثبت الثانى ولا نعنى القادر إلا ذلك
Problem: All agreed that He, exalted, is Qadir (powerful), contrary to the majority of philosophers. We have: that the dependence of the world on an agent is established. That agent is either such that the effect emanates from it with the impossibility of not emanating, or it emanates with the possibility of not emanating. The first is false because if its influence on the existence of the world is not dependent on a condition, then from its eternity follows the eternity of the world, and we have refuted that. And if it is dependent on a condition, then if that condition is eternal, the same implication returns. If it is originated, then the discussion about its origination is like the discussion about the first, and it leads to an infinite regress either simultaneously, which is impossible, or without a first, which results in events with no beginning, which is impossible. When this division is invalidated, the second is established, and we mean by Qadir nothing but that.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. Razi states the agreed-upon claim that God is Qadir (powerful), with the majority of philosophers dissenting. He then provides a proof: the world depends on an agent. That agent is either a necessitating cause (where the effect is inseparable) or a free agent (where effect and non-effect are both possible). The necessitating cause is impossible because if it has no condition, its eternity would require the world's eternity (contradicting the world's temporality). If it has a condition, that condition is either eternal (same problem) or originated, which leads to infinite regress or an infinite series of originated events, both impossible. Therefore, the agent must be a free agent, which is the meaning of Qadir.

Key Terms
قادر
مؤثر
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof assumes the world is created in time (hadith) as a premise.
Correction: The proof only assumes the world's dependence on an agent (iftiqar), not its temporal origination. The refutation of the necessitating cause relies on the impossibility of an eternal world, which is established separately.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what are the two possible types of agent for the world?
A) A necessitating cause and a free agent (Qadir)
B) An eternal cause and a temporal cause
C) A material cause and a formal cause
D) A necessary being and a contingent being

Key Takeaway
The only way to avoid logical absurdities is to affirm that the agent of the world is a free agent (Qadir), who can choose to act or not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were a necessitating cause, your every action would be compelled. Knowing that He is Qadir—able to choose—how does this shape your understanding of your own choices and responsibility before Him? Will you today truly live as if your repentance, obedience, and supplication matter to a free Lord?
?
The proof shows that an infinite regress of conditions is absurd. Yet you often postpone repentance, thinking there will always be another chance. Does that not resemble a chain of conditions with no real end? What condition are you waiting for to turn back to Allah, and can you afford to let it regress into an impossible infinity?
?
Razi refutes the philosophers' notion of a necessary emanation. Have you ever assumed that God's actions are somehow 'automatic'—that He must forgive, or must punish, or must answer your du'a? How does affirming that God is truly free (Qadir) change the way you approach Him in worship and reliance?

Razi's Response to the Necessitating Cause Objection
Razi responds to the objection that God could be a necessitating cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's refutation of the claim that an eternal agent necessarily produces an eternal effect.

Core Idea
An eternal cause does not automatically produce an eternal effect.

This passage presents an objection to the argument that God must be Qadir (powerful) rather than a mere necessitating cause. The objector suggests that if God were a necessitating cause, the world would be eternal. Razi responds by distinguishing the conditions for causation, emphasizing that the possibility of the effect is a prerequisite. This lesson unpacks his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the claim: if God were a necessitating cause (mujib), His eternity would entail the eternity of the world.
The objector tries to force Razi into admitting either that the agent is not eternal or that the world is eternal.
2
Follow the two-case response
Razi splits the problem: either the agent's existence is sound in pre-eternity or not. Trace each branch and its consequence.
The first branch accepts the eternity of the world, which is not a problem for the objector. The second branch leads to the key condition.
3
Identify the key condition
Notice that for the effect to emanate, the possibility of the effect must be present alongside the existence of the agent.
This condition blocks the automatic inference from eternal agent to eternal effect.
4
Examine the supporting analogy
Razi invokes the Ash'ari concept of Qadir: God's pre-eternal power did not necessitate the soundness of creation in pre-eternity.
The analogy shows that eternal attribute does not force eternal effect.
5
Synthesize the conclusion
Understand that the objection fails because the effect's possibility is a separate condition. Thus, God being Qadir is compatible with a temporal world.
This defends the necessity of God being Qadir over being a mere necessitating cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل ام لا يجوز أن يكون المؤثر موجبا قوله يلزم من قدمه قدم العالم . قلنا إما أن يكون صحيح الوجود فى الأزل أو لا يكون ، فإن كان الأول لم يكن قدم العالم محلا فنحن نلتزمه وإن كان الثاني كان لصحة وجوده بذاته ، وإذا كان كذلك لم يلزم من قدم المؤثر قدم العالم ، لأن صدور الأثر عن المؤثر كما يعتبر فيه وجود المؤثر يعتبر فيه إمكان الأثر ، والذى يؤيده وهو أن القادر عندك هو الذي منه الإيجاد ، والله تعالى كان قادرا في الأزل ولم يلزم من أزلية قدرته صحة الإيجاد أزلا فلما لم. يصح يلزم من القدرة الأزلية حصول الصحة في الأزل، فلم لا يجوز أن لا يلزم من وجود المؤثر وجود العالم في الأزل
If it is said: Why is it not permissible that the agent be a necessitating cause? His statement: From its eternity follows the eternity of the world. We say: It is either sound in existence in pre-eternity or not. If the first, then the eternity of the world is not a problem, and we accept it. If the second, then its existence is self-sufficient. If so, the eternity of the agent does not necessitate the eternity of the world, because the emanation of the effect from the agent, just as the existence of the agent is considered, the possibility of the effect is also considered. What supports this is that the Qadir according to you is the one from whom is the bringing into existence. And God, exalted, was Qadir in pre-eternity, yet from the pre-eternity of His power the soundness of bringing into existence in pre-eternity did not follow. So if it is not sound that from pre-eternal power the obtaining of soundness in pre-eternity follows, then why is it not permissible that from the existence of the agent the existence of the world in pre-eternity does not follow?
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an objection and response. The objector argues that the agent might be a necessitating cause, so the argument's inference from agent to Qadir fails. Razi responds by distinguishing two possibilities for the agent: it could be sound in existence in pre-eternity or not. If it is sound in pre-eternity, then the eternity of the world is entailed, but that is not a problem to the objector. If it is not sound in pre-eternity, then its existence is self-sufficient, and the effect's possibility is required; thus the agent's eternity does not automatically make the effect eternal. He reinforces this by analogy: God's power was pre-eternal yet did not necessitate the soundness of creation in pre-eternity. Therefore, the existence of the agent does not necessitate the existence of the world in pre-eternity.

Key Terms
موجب
قادر
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God is eternal and the cause of the world, the world must be eternal.
Correction: Razi shows that the effect's possibility must be present for the effect to exist; an eternal cause does not automatically produce an eternal effect.

Checkpoint
What is the key point in Razi's response to the necessitating cause objection?
A) The effect's possibility must be present for the effect to exist.
B) The agent's existence alone necessitates the effect.
C) The agent must be originated.
D) The world is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Razi argues that the possibility of the effect, not just the existence of the agent, determines whether the effect is eternal, so God being eternal does not force the world to be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power does not force His creation, what does that mean for your prayers? Do you ask out of habit or with true awareness that He is not compelled to answer?
?
When you reflect on your own existence, do you see yourself as a necessary outcome of causes or as an act of free divine will? How does that change your gratitude?
?
Razi argues that possibility matters. Are you living as if God's power is constrained by what you think is possible? What would change if you truly believed He can do what He wills, with no necessity?
